And I suppose one can forgive a brain surgeon for being detail-oriented!<br /><br />This book rang true on so many levels regarding Alexander's discoveries while comatose, as well as the painful beliefs described from before his illness, including feelings of separation from God and doubt about his own self-worth on some levels. Other teachers have said some version of this: everything we need to know already exists within us and simply needs to be given attention or reawakened. There was scarcely a paragraph in this book that didn't sound like something I already Know (capital K) inside.  It definitely reawakened a number of alternately exciting and comforting corners of my own self.<br /><br />I hope Alexander's unblinking account of his unique and eerily coincidental (example: his wife is friends with a person who does telepathy with coma patients) experience will awaken the souls of many in the medical field as well as outside.  He said, in different words, something echoed in the teachings of Abraham-Hicks: one cannot perceive what one isn't a vibrational match to.  I think this story has the potential to help humanity rise to higher levels of awareness and perception of the non-physical world.  What was new and useful to me, in contrast to other metaphysical/channeling teachers I've listened to, was Alexander's simple yet profound explanation of the purpose of evil on earth. There are many take-home messages in this book; to me the one about evil's place in our world is the most memorable.<br /><br />Get this book, read it and pass it on.

B008U0FJF8|2.0|I downloaded this CD after hearing an NPR interview with the artist. I was intrigued by his classical backround and by the inclusion of a few nice sounding snippets from the album. If I had known however that the snippets essentially WERE the album, I would not have pressed the 'open file' tab quite so fast.<br />If the artist was indeed classically trained he does not display it here and the album is most disappointing as a compositional statement. It consists of a series of simplistic chordal and/or melodic expositions. Sometimes two are strung together to expand the piece, more often emphatically not. In terms of thematic development, forget about it...there just isn't any. He relies on his soloists to propel the music forward, but there's not enough musical depth to float the improvisational boat so it goes nowhere. Therefore the pieces tend to be short and they end abruptly with no real sense of conclusion. Did anybody ever mention the word: coda? I think not. One cut towards the end of the album is a riff on one arpeggiated minor augmented piano chord which leads into a drum solo. This is good....he's a percussionist....at last something with at least a little passion! Then, instead of trying to segue back to the piano for a proper ending, it just suddenly stops with the drum solo. He's almost like a child with a whole box of Crayolas. He has no idea what to do with the chromatic tools at his disposal, so he just scribbles small patches of color on a sheet of paper, then he calls it art. It's not art! In order to do abstract expressionism you gotta be able to limn an accurate torso.<br />I'm not prepared to throw this CD in the trashcan. In it's favor, however amateurishly minimalist the pieces are they do display a soft and sort of haunting lyricism. It seems to be excellent sound by which to fall asleep. Of course, that's almost as bad as saying it's also good for going up and down in an elevator. But it does earn it a rating of sorts. With all the junk that's out there, that's actually saying something.....

Both craft records that sound rigid and at times, harmonic.  \\"Vanitas\\" pushes their legacy forward by remaining close to their sound, yet infecting it with diversity.<br /><br />Only a few months after \\"Passion's\\" released, Vitrol announced that their forthcoming record, \\"Vanitas\\" was done.  Like most, I said, \\"That was fast.\\"  By no means does it feel rushed - A.N. only records when they are ready.  So what did the six months or so bring? Right off the bat, you will notice the organic nature of \\"Vanitas.\\"  Whatever didn't work was discarded in favor of \\"just vibing it out.\\"  There are bits of electronic elements sprinkled to push atmosphere.  The pace of the record is immaculate - mid-tempo intros are used early to build suspense (Todos Somos Humanos) which is only amplified by Vitols flawless cleans in \\"In Coelo Quies, Tout Finis Ici Bas.\\"  There are particular tracks that utilize a bit of \\"groove.\\"  I don't label A.N. as \\"such and such genre of band.\\"  A.N. is A.N.  \\"Vanitas\\" solidifies their sound while making experimental tweaks that pay off big time.<br /><br />Vitrol is insane.  I firmly believe \\"Vanitas\\" showcases his best work.  His cleans are bar-none, the best.  It's such a dichotomy.  He goes from guttural lows to piercing highs; to these elemental cleans(\\"To Spite the Face\\").  My personal favorite - \\"Forging Towards the Sunset\\" is just as anthemic as \\"Oil Upon the Sores of Lepers.\\"  The verses inevitably lead up to one of the best clean vocals sections I've ever heard.  Album closer \\"A Metaphor for the Dead\\" is compensated by the chugging of \\"Feeding the Beast,\\" and rapture of \\"Of Fire & ____ Pigs.\\"  It begins with haunting tones, then quickly dives into Mick's handy-work.  The song skirts closely to harmonic.  Vitrols cleans hit - you'd swear that they're unreal.  It's abeautiful choir of rhythm and tone. \\"A Metaphor for the Dead\\" closes the album off with resonance.<br /><br />Mick Kenney is by far one of the best guitarists in the business.  The riffs and sheer technicalities electrifying his digits are unmatched (\\"Make Glorious the Embrace of Saturn\\").  I proud \\"Vanitas\\" demonstrates sparse elements of groove.  Certain melodies are fresh and sit firmly in place next to their grinding riffs.  That's not to say A.N. have gone softer - just more experimental.  \\"Todos Somos Humanos\\" plunges audiences into fathoms known by fans.  Let's not forget the opener - \\"The Blood Dimmed Tide.\\"  After chilling spoken words; an onslaught - a barrage of grinding riffs similar to spear heads colliding with armor plating begins.<br /><br />Now I enlighten you all!  I am sure no one will make these connections but it is necessary.  I consider \\"Vanitas\\" to be a \\"fourth horsemen.\\"  Mick Kenney has had his hands into a bunch of projects this past year.  Where he goes - so do his influences.  Mick formed a band with Brandan Schiepatti called \\"Suffer Well.\\"  He described it as \\"Bleeding Through meets Anaal Nathrahk.\\"  You can tell by the way the album sounds, that it couldn't be more true.  Next - and most importantly, Bleeding Through's \\"The Great Fire\\" was produced by Mick.  That's why the album has DNA of A.N.  The guitar tuning, the grinds, the sharp blast beats, and shorter length.  The album plays off Bleeding Through's strength and religion to hardcore(review in my profile).  Next - I Am War's \\"Outlive You All\\" was also produced by Mick.  Listen to the riffs and tuning - it has residues of Mick's own hand - rigid and scathing.  Now we have \\"Vanitas\\" - the fourth member of this chronology.  Within the past year Mick has been in the shadows helping other bands only for him to come full circle.  Knowing this makes the record more enjoyable.  You will notice certain elements that - \\"Hey, that sounds like that one part from...\\"  Not that any of the records are cut and paste, but each has some residue of another.  \\"Vanitas\\" is the crescendo.  All hail the \\"Serpent's Breath.\\"

He has rarely disappointed and oftentimes exceeds my high expectations.<br /><br />With the Racketeer, at least for me, he misses the mark.  Please read carefully as my critic is mostly tied up with one pet peeve of mine and may not be a show stopper for other readers.<br /><br />Grisham delivers his usual page turning suspense, interesting scenarios which move with the usual fluid speed of the genre.  He also creates a believable set of characters who are both familiar while being unique at the same time.  The plot set-up also is a stroke of genius.  It will definitely keep you guessing as how it will play out especially about half way through the novel when you realize the story is not going in the direction you had been led to believe.<br /><br />And this what destroyed the story for me.  I don't mind being mislead, surprised or being outsmarted (happens often).  My issue is these are not the things i expect from my main character.  Grisham uses the unreliable narrator as his main character - though this is a valid point of view, it is a troublesome selection in a mystery, especially one structured like this.  It also happens to be my least favorite narration form.<br /><br />Essentially, by utilizing the unreliable narrator everything you are led to be believe in the first half of the book is either untrue or suspect.  This may be a nice surprise for some readers for a mystery reader this is very unsettling especially because such a skilled novelist as Grisham he has displayed time and time again the ability to surprise, create plot twists and deliver the unexpected without resorting to an unreliable narrator.<br /><br />End of the day, the Racketeer is a page turner - i finished it in two days - however, at least for me, i've come to expect better from Grisham.  (note:  i will still preorder his next legal thriller - still a fan).

0060935464|5.0|My son's 9th-grade class was assigned \\"To Kill a Mockingbird\\" in their English course. It has been over twenty years since I had read Harper Lee's classic and only novel. The small, Alabama town of Maycomb is in the grips of the Great Depression. Jim Crow is alive and well doing its worse by oppressing African-Americans. The story is seen through the eyes of tomboy Scout Finch. It highlights her growth from a six-to-nine-year-old girl. Ms. Lee created a protagonist who still had a child's innocence about the world around her. She isn't just confused about the illogical nature of prejudice but also by many of the social norms of small town America. Scout's dad, the now iconic Atticus Finch, is a poor, 50ish, intelligent lawyer of reason and high morals struggling to raise his daughter and their 13-year-old son Jem. He fortunately has the help of an intelligent black maid named Calpurnia. The climax of the story finds Atticus defending Tom Robinson, an African-American accused of assaulting a white woman.<br /><br />Ms. Lee, who was born in Alabama, clearly expresses her disdain for many of the South's cultural mores. The story not only shows the actual manner in which blacks were treated, but ridicules the Southern obsession with family lineage and how your place in society is based purely on which hoo hoo you popped out of during birth. The story has some wonderfully colorful and highly believable characters. It harkens back to a tougher, simpler time and how most of these folks tried to live god-fearing, decent lives, but don't have the intelligence or courage to treat blacks as human beings; let alone equals. The N-word is appropriately used quite frequently in the book due to the nature of the times and location of the novel.<br /><br />Ms. Lee's book is a well-written story that deserves its wide readership. It is also still very relevant in 2012. It would've been inconceivable to 1930 Southerners that less than eighty years later an African-American would be elected President of the United States. The reelection of President Obama just occurred two days ago and some of the very vulgar stereotypes expressed about him (especially on such mediums as Twitter) shows racism is still very much alive and well throughout America. Prejudice manifests itself in many ways. \\"To Kill a Mockingbird\\"  humanizes the destructive nature that prejudice causes to the victims, perpetrators and bystanders. A great, sometimes funny, suspenseful work of art that challenges readers to look at themselves in the mirror.ected President of the United States. B00003OO3O|5.0|UFO is a Blues based hard rock band from Britain formed back in 1969 by Phil Mogg, Andy Parker, and Pete Way. Michael Schenker joined the band in 1973 and so began a six year stint of fabulous creative music and the release of five studio albums and one live double package.<br /><br />At the core of the band is Michael Schenker on lead guitar. Phil Mogg on vocals, Pete Way on Bass, and Andy Parker on drums.<br /><br />Force It was released in 1975. It has an aggressive driving guitar sound full of blistering riffs. \\"Force It\\" spawned 5 major concert favorites, Let It Roll, Shoot Shoot, Out In The Street, Mother Mary, and This Kid's. All of them showing up later on the band's signature live album, Strangers In The Night.\\"<br /><br />Their music was very much underrated for the time period. They had one of the strongest guitarists on the move at the time and the album \\"Force It\\" was their first march into rock stardom from their earlier bluesy offerings. It also helped them penetrate the foreign markets and earn them acclaim at home which seemed reserved for bands like Led Zeppelin at the time.<br /><br />There isn't one bad tune in the bunch. Mogg is an excellent vocalist providing excellent melodies to complement Schenker's endless six string arsenal.<br /><br />UFO are one of heavy metal's earliest and greatest bands and this release is the beginning of their best creative period. UFO would gain huge success over the years and this album in my opinion started it all.

B007SGLZP8|3.0|While conceding that I have enjoyed many John Grisham novels, and also conceding that I liked The Racketeer enough to give it 3 stars, there is still a lingering disappointment that this was the best Grisham could do this year. Readers look forward to his really good legal thrillers, and to finish this one only moderately satisfied means we have to wait longer still for him to do his really good stuff. It's a cute story, but the deck seemed so stacked that the suspension of belief required to enjoy it felt really forced. Perhaps Grisham is ready to retire to Antigua and needed a few more bucks before he could go...but, what's he going to read when he gets there? Surely even he wants to read only the best.

B007SGLZP8|3.0|Halfway through the book, I thought I had accidentally switched to another title on my Kindle.  The story line I had been reading disappeared, and the \\"hero\\" was suddenly involved with a completely set of characters and a completely different plot.  It's all explained in the end, but that's part of what annoyed me about this book.  Things happen for no apparent reason, only to be justified by additional information from the narrator a few pages later.  It felt sloppy and rushed to me, as if Grisham had dashed this one off without thinking about it too much (a view that's arguably supported by the Afterward in which he proudly says he made everything up).  As a result, I didn't care about any of the characters.  Nor was I particularly intrigued by the plot.<br /><br />Like all Grisham novels, this book is very readable.  But unlike his earlier works it's forgotten as soon as it's finished.  This is a trifle, a well-written bit of nothing.
